Title: NYSE Plans Texas Exchange as Financial Firms Flock to State
URL: https://www.insurancejournal.com/news/southcentral/2025/02/12/811807.htm
Time Published: 2025-02-12T16:58:19Z
Full Content:
The New York Stock Exchange plans to start an equities exchange in Texas, the latest firm seeking a slice of the financial services industry in a state where the taxes are lower and regulation looser. NYSE said it will reincorporate its NYSE Chicago operations in Texas and will launch the fully electronic exchange in Dallas, pending regulatory filings. The exchange will serve companies from Texas and around the world, it said. NYSEâ€™s move underscores the heightened allure of Texas for corporations and financial firms seeking to benefit from a more relaxed regulatory environment than blue states like New York and California. Dallas is host to the Texas Stock Exchange, which counts BlackRock Inc. and Citadel Securities among its backers and plans to begin trading in early 2026. Nasdaq last year reorganized its listings business into three regional divisions including Texas. â€œAs the state with the largest number of NYSE listings, representing over $3.7 trillion in market value for our community, Texas is a market leader in fostering a pro-business atmosphere,â€ NYSE President Lynn Martin said in a statement. The NYSEâ€™s plans give another boost to the Dallas-Fort Worth area, which already has more finance workers than Chicago or Los Angeles, trailing only New York. Goldman Sachs Group Inc. is building a new campus in Dallas that will house about 5,000 employees. â€œWith the launch of NYSE Texas, we will expand our financial might in the United States and cement our great state as an economic powerhouse on the global stage,â€ Texas Governor Greg Abbott said. Although the state is known for its business-friendly approach, the Texas Stock Exchange has faced some other challenges. It was already contending with an uphill climb to secure listings. Its promises to avoid what could be seen as political requirements, like board composition requirements, have lost punch as companies have begun rolling back diversity and environmental pledges. It would also need to bite off business from private equity. â€œTheyâ€™re not only competing against the New York Stock Exchange and Nasdaq,â€ said Andrew Silverman, an analyst with Bloomberg Intelligence. â€œTheyâ€™re also competing against Blackstone. Theyâ€™re also competing against Apollo. Theyâ€™re also competing against Berkshire Hathaway.â€ TXSE Group Inc., parent company of the proposed Texas Stock Exchange, recently closed its initial fundraising round at $161 million and said TXSE has filed for registration as a bourse with the US Securities and Exchange Commission. â€œWe are committed to closely aligning with issuers and investors to provide a premier venue for listing and a world-class platform for trading,â€ a spokesperson for TXSE said in a statement. â€œWe have known all along that Texas is the best place to do business.â€ NYSE and its biggest rival Nasdaq dominate the IPO market, which is rebounding after a lengthy slump on geopolitical uncertainty, inflation and higher interest rates. Nasdaq Chief Executive Officer Adena Friedman said last month she expects a strong environment for IPOs in the second quarter and rest of the year. NYSEâ€™s move to Dallas is â€œgoing to bring more financial firms with it, and force Texas to reinforce its infrastructure,â€ said David Choate, chief operating officer of Dallas-based brokerage firm CAPIS. â€œYouâ€™re always wanting to be on the cutting edge of technology if youâ€™re hosting financial firms like exchanges,â€ he said. Title: Blackrock CEO Larry Fink Gave His 'Diagnosis' Of Retirement Crisis: Rely On Social Security Alone And 'You're Going To Be Living In Poverty'
URL: https://finance.yahoo.com/news/blackrock-ceo-larry-fink-gave-144521903.html
Time Published: 2025-02-12T14:45:21Z
Full Content:
We are experiencing some temporary issues. The market data on this page is currently delayed. Please bear with us as we address this and restore your personalized lists. BlackRock CEO Larry Fink isn't sugarcoating the problem: retirement in America is broken. In a March 2024 interview with Bloomberg, David Westin got straight to the point, asking Fink for his take on the crisis: "Give us your diagnosis of that problem." Fink clarified that millions of Americans aren't financially prepared for their later years. "We have still 57 million Americans who don't have any savings or any retirement plan," he stated. And if those people think Social Security alone will carry them through, Fink had a blunt reality check: "If that's all you have when you retire, you're going to be living in poverty, below the poverty line." Don't Miss: Many donâ€™t know there are tax benefits when buying a unit as an investment â€” Hereâ€™s how to invest in real estate by mirroring BlackRock's big move Many are using retirement income calculators to check if theyâ€™re on pace â€” hereâ€™s a breakdown on whatâ€™s behind this formula. Fink's wake-up call wasn't just theoretical. In his 2024 annual letter to shareholders, he reflected on his experience handling his parents' finances after his mother passed away. He was surprised at how much they had saved despite their modest income, a stark contrast to the dire state many retirees find themselves in today. According to Fink, the crux of the issue is that the entire retirement system is outdated. "Most Americans retired between 60 and 62 then, but most Americans passed away at 67," he explained. "Today, statistically, a couple 60 years old in good health â€“ one of them is going to live over 90." With people living decades longer, retirement savings must stretch further, yet most aren't prepared. Advances in medicine compound this longevity crisis. "The miracles of technology ... are extending life," Fink said, referencing breakthroughs in treatments for heart disease, kidney disease and even dementia. But while medicine is evolving, financial planning isn't keeping up. "There is not a dialogue in America ... about can we afford that longevity?" Trending: Can you guess how many Americans successfully retire with $1,000,000 saved? The percentage may shock you. Fink believes fixing retirement requires two things: conversation and action. "We solve problems through conversation," he said. But when it comes to retirement, "we have no conversation." He stressed the need for a global â€“ and national â€“ dialogue to reevaluate retirement age, savings strategies and investment approaches. One potential fix? Using capital markets to boost retirement savings. Fink pointed to Japan, where a recent policy change doubled the amount of tax-deductible retirement contributions. The result? A 30% surge in the Japanese stock market, driven by long-term investment. "Not only does it give financial returns for those who are retiring and saving for retirement, but it's a big foundation for domestic companies," he explained. With Social Security on shaky ground, Fink suggested a controversial idea: investing the Social Security trust fund in long-term assets. "Right now in Congress, a number of senators and congressmen are talking about rehabilitating our Social Security pool and maybe contributing a big block of money into it," he noted. The U.S. system, he said, is a "pay-as-you-go" model, unlike countries such as Australia, where retirement funds are structured differently to ensure sustainability. As a baby boomer himself, Fink acknowledged that his generation has benefited from economic prosperity, but he questioned whether they've done enough to secure a stable future for younger generations. "We were born at a great economic moment," he said. "We all have a responsibility to try to recreate that environment for our grandchildren." His message was clear: Americans need to save more, invest smarter and rethink their approach to retirement. Because as Fink put it, "We need to have a conversation." That conversation shouldn't just be national â€“ it should also be personal. With people living longer and the retirement landscape shifting, now is the time to consult a financial advisor to ensure you're on track. Whether adjusting your investment strategy, maximizing your savings or finding ways to generate income in retirement, getting professional guidance can help you retire on your terms â€“ without relying solely on Social Security. Title: Bitcoin May See Gains from Soft U.S. CPI, Major Risk-On Surge in BTC Appears Unlikely
URL: https://www.coindesk.com/markets/2025/02/12/bitcoin-may-see-gains-from-soft-u-s-cpi-major-risk-on-surge-in-btc-appears-unlikely
Time Published: 2025-02-12T06:45:41Z
Full Content:
A soft U.S. inflation report later Wednesday will likely bode well for risk assets, including bitcoin (BTC). But those expecting bullish fireworks may be disappointed. The Labor Department will publish January's consumer price index (CPI) report on Wednesday at 13:30 UTC. It's expected to show that the cost of living increased by 0.3% month-on-month in January, slowing down from December's 0.4% rise, according to Reuters estimates tracked by FXStreet. The annualized figure is expected to match December's 2.9% reading. The core inflation, which strips out the volatile food and energy component, is forecast to have risen to 0.3% month-over-month from 0.2%, resulting in an annualized reading of 3.1%, down from December's 3.2%. Lower-than-expected data, particularly the core figure, will likely bolster expectations for further Federal Reserve (Fed) interest rate cuts, which could lead to lower Treasury yields and a weaker dollar index, ultimately boosting demand for riskier assets. According to CME's FedWatch tool, the market currently estimates a 54% chance that the Fed will either cut interest rates once or not at all this year. While a potential adjustment in Fed rate cuts could lift BTC, it is unlikely to be the sole catalyst for a breakout from the ongoing consolidation between $90,000 and $110,000. This is due to forward-looking market metrics indicating higher inflation in the coming months amid trade war fears, suggesting that the Fed may have a limited window to implement aggressive rate cuts. Data tracked by Mott Capital Management shows that two-year inflation swaps have climbed to nearly 2.8%, the highest since early 2023. The five-year swap is exhibiting a similar trend. Higher inflation swaps indicate that the market is expecting inflation rates to rise in the future, prompting investors to pay a higher premium to protect themselves against potential purchasing power loss by entering into swap contracts tied to CPI. In other words, the ongoing uptick in these metrics indicate that the progress in inflation toward the Fed's 2% target has stalled, and price pressures are likely to increase over the coming years, probably due to Trump's tariffs. Plus, some investment banks believe a soft January CPI reading won't see the Fed move away from its hawkish rate guidance. In his testimony to Congress Tuesday, Chairman Jerome Powell said the central bank is in no hurry to cut rates. "We donâ€™t expect that progress on inflation will be enough to prompt additional interest rate cuts from the Fed this year," RBC's weekly note said, adding that January's report will show limited easing in price pressures. BlackRock said the persistent services inflation will keep the Fed from cutting rates. "We get U.S. CPI for January this week. Even as Decemberâ€™s CPI report showed signs of inflation pressures easing, wage growth remains above the level that would allow inflation to recede back to the Federal Reserveâ€™s 2% target, in our view. We see persistent services inflation forcing the Fed to keep rates higher for longer," BlackRock said. Lastly, BTC may move closer to the lower end of its $90K-$110K trading range should the CPI print hotter than expected. Omkar Godbole is a Co-Managing Editor on CoinDesk's Markets team based in Mumbai, holds a masters degree in Finance and a Chartered Market Technician (CMT) member. Omkar previously worked at FXStreet, writing research on currency markets and as fundamental analyst at currency and commodities desk at Mumbai-based brokerage houses. Omkar holds small amounts of bitcoin, ether, BitTorrent, tron and dot. About Contact Policies

Title: Who Owns the World? The Boom-Bust Bailout Process that Placed Nations in Debt
URL: https://www.globalresearch.ca/who-owns-world-boom-bust-bailout-process-placed-nations-debt/5879666
Time Published: 2025-02-11T15:42:36Z
Full Content:
There are systemic aspects about the banking, monetary, and economic system that are not taught in the schools and universities of the world and are rarely discussed on corporate owned news and media networks. Knowledge of these aspects is absolutely essential for everyone in the world that wishes to understand how the economic world â€˜actuallyâ€™ works and how worldwide society has been brought to the brink of financial ruin (currently almost all governments of the world are in vast debt) while the vast resources of human productivity and of nature are continually exploited by a small group of people that control these systems. See also the book Demonic Economics and the Tricks of the Bankers. This article explores: Without GDP growth the (privately owned) debt-money banking system fails. The real reason governments prioritise GDP growth is so that sufficient tax monies can be collected so that interest can be paid to the international banking system. Governments often maintain that the ultimate purpose of economic GDP growth is in fact to improve wellbeing. This is not in fact so. John Jopling (RIP) of the Foundation for the Economics of Sustainability wrote in 2003: â€œThe real reason why governments regard growth as desirable is that, with a debt-based money system, if the economy does not grow, it collapses. This is something all politicians are naturally and rightly extremely keen to avoid. Growth is an absolute imperative imposed on governments by the nature of the current money system. Thus, it is in the nature of the money system, not the choice of government, that growth must be maintained.â€[1] Governments are buried under the lie, they do not admit or have the awareness that the need for GDP growth is imposed by the debt-money system controlled by private banks nor that the creation of debt money by private banks is unnecessary and is against the public interest (because governments could create and issue debt-free money themselves as has been done in the past). It is rarely acknowledged by politicians that the main reason for the constant drive for GDP growth is to pay interest to the banking system. The Foundation for the Economics of Sustainability has stated: â€œThe way in which the global economic system is designed automatically ensures that the economy operates in such a way that: a. inequality is bound to increase, b. the economy is unstable and c. the economy is blind to the limits of natural resources and the need for humanity to live in symbiosis with the rest of the natural world.â€ â€“ The Foundation for the Economics of Sustainabilit[2] GDP growth is prioritised by governments and debt-money is the basis of the banking system â€“ yet both are significant drivers of environmental degradation, resource depletion, and social inequity. A government prioritises growth, yet whether it is â€˜goodâ€™ growth or â€˜badâ€™ growth is not the focus (good growth would not impact on environmental and social resilience.) The pseudo-science of neo-classical economics (that all governments adhere to) proposes that increased GDP growth can reduce pollution in what is called the environmental Kuznets curve (EKC). This EKC argument is false. The EKC posits that pollution increases with economic growth in the early stages of development and that beyond a certain level of development the trend reverses, and economic growth improves environmental conditions by creating the resources to do so. However, the EKC has never been validated. Vastly excessive consumerism has been required to keep the system from derailing. The debt-money system increases and reduces the availability credit at will often creating â€˜boom, bust and bailoutâ€™ cycles â€“ this means that the economic system is unstable by nature. If sufficient loans are not repaid to a commercial bank it will become insolvent. This has happened in many countries, for example in various countries in Europe during the banking crisis of 2008. . The collapse of Lehman Brothers (headquarters pictured), the fourth-largest U.S. investment bank, on September 15, 2008, is often considered the climax of the 2008 financial crisis. (Licensed under CC BY-SA 3.0) . [Aside: Bear in mind that these private banks never held the original monies in the first place, and, the cruel bait and switch is that it is actually the people that are the grantors of credit when they sign a mortgage or loan (a promise to pay), however, the bank typically never pays back the grantor of the credit. Including interest one typically pays the bank about twice the amount of the loan or mortgage. Yet, the bank does not pay equity for that promissory note, and presumes that we have abandoned our securities]. Typically a national government then intervenes to bail out those commercial banks, being under pressure to do so from the international banking system. Furthermore, by controlling the availability of credit the private banking cartel created boom-bust-bailout cycles, at will, which placed nations in further debt. For example, the European Central Bank (ECB) exerted pressure on the Irish government to bail out private banks and unsecured bondholders in 2010. In 2012 RTE, Irelandâ€™s National Television Service reported that the ECB informed an Irish Government Minister that â€œa bomb will go off in Dublinâ€ if Anglo bondholders are not paid. â€œHe [Minister for Transport and Tourism, Leo Varadkar] said that the Troika told the Government that â€œwe donâ€™t want you to default on these payments, it is your decision ultimately but a bomb will go off; and the bomb will go off in Dublin and not in Frankfurt.â€ â€“ RTE reporting Minister Varadkarâ€™s comments 22nd January 2012. [Note: The Troika is a term used to describe the European Commission (EC), the European Central Bank (ECB) and the International Monetary Fund (IMF).] Furthermore, a letter was sent by the ECB to pressure the Irish Government to accept a bailout. In that letter then ECB head Jean-Claude Trichet told Ireland in November 2010 that it would not extend further emergency funding to the countryâ€™s banks if Dublin did not sign up to a bailout, according to the letter which was finally released after years of lobbying. The so-called global banking crises of 2008 represented an opportunity for a re-evaluation of the values that our banking system and economic system are based on. Moreover, it represented an ideal opportunity for transition toward a more sustainable, resilient, just, and, perhaps even, a more ethical society. Alas, this opportunity was spurned, and almost all governments bailed out the banks. This results in increased taxes, national austerity measures and/or the privatisation of national assets due to conditionalities on credit. For example, in Ireland the government must pay around â‚¬6 billion to â‚¬10 billion per annum in interest on the national debt of â‚¬235 billon[3] â€“ a significant portion of this debt (â‚¬85 billion) was incurred due to bailing out private commercial banks in Ireland in 2008[4]. To understand the magnitude of this debt if you convert into U.S. dollars and lay $1 bills on top of each other they would make a pile 28,581 km, or 17,760 miles high. These debts will never be fully repaid and the annual interest payments alone are, in effect, a never-ending shackle of debt servitude and a form of slavery for the Irish people. Similar bailout situations have occurred in many other countries worldwide. â€œThere are two ways to conquer and enslave a nation. One is by the sword. The other is by debt.â€ â€“ U.S. President John Adams The banking system can and does control the availability of credit (i.e., debt-money loans). It can expand or contract the availability of credit in a nation or worldwide. Over the past decades the more credit that is available the more an economy is likely to grow (there are also other factors including the availability of a cheap energy source, such as oil). When the availability of credit is contracted/reduced by the banking system the money supply shrinks, the availability of money to repay loans plus interest is reduced, foreclosures begin to occur and the economy may start to shrink rather than grow. This expansion and contraction of credit is known as the business cycle. â€œThe fact that the necessary growth can be achieved only by increasing the total level of debt makes the economy heavily dependent on confidenceâ€¦ The economy therefore constantly moves between boom and bust; it is systemically unstable.â€ â€“ John Joplin and Roy Madron, authors of â€˜Gaian Democraciesâ€™[5] â€œThe bankrupt country must borrow from international banks and the IMF, which impose a condition of debt relief that the national government may not issue its own money. Title: Archer Aviation raises $300 million in BlackRock-backed funding
URL: https://finance.yahoo.com/news/archer-aviation-raises-300-million-133628091.html
Time Published: 2025-02-11T13:36:28Z
Full Content:
We are experiencing some temporary issues. The market data on this page is currently delayed. Please bear with us as we address this and restore your personalized lists. (Reuters) - Air-taxi maker Archer Aviation said on Tuesday it has raised $300 million in a funding round that consisted of institutional investors including accounts managed by BlackRock. Archer expects the capital raise to help it accelerate the development of its hybrid aircraft platform and further reinforce its balance sheet. "We are raising additional capital to help us invest in critical capabilities like composites and batteries to help enable us to capture this opportunity and more," CEO Adam Goldstein said. The additional capital brings Archer's total liquidity to about $1 billion currently, the company said on Tuesday. The company's statement did not disclose the valuation at which the new capital was raised. The latest fundraising comes amid a cash crunch in the electric vertical takeoff and landing (eVTOL) industry, driven by technological and regulatory challenges. However, analysts believe Archer is well positioned to endure these difficulties and achieve certification. The company previously raised $430 million in December through an equity offering that had defense technology company Anduril and existing investors such as United Airlines and Stellantis, as well as new backers such as Wellington Management and Abu Dhabi investment holding company 2PointZero, participate in the fundraising. Santa Clara, California-based Archer said in its preliminary fourth-quarter results that its adjusted operating expenses were in line with its forecast range of $95 million to $110 million. It also said it does not expect its total adjusted operating expenses for the first quarter of 2025 to materially increase above its Q4 guided range. Title: Archer Aviation doubles down on defense aircraft with fresh $300M | TechCrunch

The raise brings Archerâ€™s total funding to around $3.36 billion. This fresh capital comes off the back of a $430 million round in December to fund its new Archer Defense program. As part of that program, Archer signed an exclusive deal with weapons manufacturer Anduril to jointly develop a hybrid gas-and-electric-powered VTOL aircraft for critical defense applications. Together, the two are targeting a program of record from the Department of Defense, which is a budgeted acquisition program with guaranteed funding over a set period. â€œAs we dug into the work we were doing on the defense front, we realized that the market was a lot larger than we initially expected, both in terms of scope as well as timing,â€ Nikhil Goel, Archerâ€™s chief commercial officer, told TechCrunch. â€œWeâ€™re the only company in the space that I think is targeting a sizable defense program of record,â€ Goel continued. â€œSo we really want to be strategic with the investments weâ€™re making and go full steam ahead on this.â€ Rivals in the space like Joby Aviation and Beta Technologies also have military contracts to test their aircraft for surveillance, logistics, and reconnaissance missions. Archer has such contracts with the military, but what itâ€™s chasing now via the program of record is guaranteed funding, a path to scale, and a serious competitive moat. Goel confirmed that the $300 million from investors will mainly be used to accelerate the work Archer is doing with Anduril to build a hybrid craft (VTOL), though he didnâ€™t share any updates on the companyâ€™s bid with the DOD. Archerâ€™s decision comes at a moment of industry momentum. The Trump administration has vowed to â€œrapidly field emerging technologiesâ€ like AI, drones, and counter-drone systems to modernize the military. The very qualities that make eVTOLs perfect for urban and regional flight are also attractive for defense use cases. Cruising at 300 feet, Archer Aviationâ€™s electric aircraft, Midnight, makes less noise than a passing car on the highway. In an urban environment, it blends into other transportation sounds in a way that helicopters cannot. â€œThe sound profile is why we are so well positioned to [build aircraft] for defense,â€ Goel said. â€œIf you look at the traditional helicopters that the defense industry uses, theyâ€™re very loud and have very noticeable heat signatures. And so that makes helicopters not a great fit for more discreet missions.â€ Archerâ€™s Midnight is built with 12 sets of engines and propellers â€“ six in the front, six in the back. That distributed propulsion among smaller rotors that spin slightly slower â€” rather than a single large main rotor and tail rotor that operate at high speeds â€” creates much less noise. VTOLs are also designed to transition from a vertical lift to a winged horizontal flight like an airplane. When in forward flight, the Midnight generates all the lift from the wing, rather than from downward thrust, which also reduces overall rotor noise, Archerâ€™s CEO and founder Adam Goldstein told TechCrunch during a recent flight demonstration. While Archer is gunning to supply the defense industry with aircraft, the company still intends to launch its first limited commercial air taxi network in late 2025 in the United Arab Emirates. In 2026, Archer says it will expand air taxi services to several other cities and countries, including Los Angeles, San Francisco, New York, South Korea, and India. The company has partnered with major airlines to facilitate air taxi networks like United, Southwest, and IndiGo. In November 2024, a joint venture from Japan Airlines and Sumitomo conditionally agreed to purchase up to $500 million worth of electric aircraft from Archer. But 2026 isnâ€™t that far away, and Archer has pushed out its timelines before. Thatâ€™s partly because Archer is still working toward validating the safety of its eVTOLs and securing the necessary certification from the Federal Aviation Administration. In the U.S., eVTOL companies need to secure type certification to approve the design of an aircraft, production certification to prove they can mass-produce a vehicle that meets its approved design, and airworthiness certification to ensure an aircraft is safe for flying. Goel says Archer is far along in the process for those certifications but has yet to receive any of them. Nor has Archer flown with a pilot in its aircraft yet, which is a necessary step toward testing the aircraft with passengers. He adds that Archer will put a pilot in one of its Midnights â€œimminently.â€ The process of certifying aircraft and scaling production is an expensive one. Construction on Archerâ€™s Georgia factory, built with its strategic investor, Stellantis, is nearly complete, with production expected to begin this quarter. Archer hopes to build 650 aircraft annually by 2030. For this year, though, Archerâ€™s goal is to produce eight to 10 aircraft between the Georgia facility and its prototype facility in California. Title: Archer Aviation raises $300M from Blackrock to expand defense sector focus
URL: https://siliconangle.com/2025/02/11/archer-aviation-raises-200m-blackrock-wellington-expand-defense-sector-focus/
Time Published: 2025-02-11T13:30:03Z
Full Content:
UPDATED 08:30 EST / FEBRUARY 11 2025 by Duncan Riley Electric vertical takeoff and landing aircraft company Archer Aviation Inc. announced today that it has raised $300 million in new funding via an equity capital raise. The $300 million in funding, raised through a securities purchase agreement, came from Blackrock Inc. and other leading institutional investors. The funding will be used to strengthen Archerâ€™s financial position and allow the company to accelerate the development of its hybrid aircraft platform, particularly for defense applications. While perhaps better known for its attempts to bring a flying taxi to market â€” which it is still pursuing â€” Archer has more recently shifted much of its focus to the defense sector. The company announced that it had signed a partnership with Anduril Industries Inc., a startup active in the defense sector, in December, alongside an announcement that it had raised $430 million to develop military aircraft. Archerâ€™s main offering, be it one still under development, is an electric flying taxi dubbed Midnight. The aircraft offers vertical takeoff and landing and is powered by propellers that can cover up to 100 miles per trip at a top speed of 150 miles per hour. Notably, Archer signed a $142 million contract to deliver six Midnights to the U.S. Air Force in July 2023. The aircraft, which can carry approximately 1,000-pound payloads, offers the U.S. military a rapid response aircraft with effectiveness across a wide range of mission profiles, from personnel transport and logistics support to rescue operations and more. As part of its shift into defense, Archer also launched a dedicated unit, Archer Defense, to develop next-generation aircraft for defense applications. The first product from the division is planned to be a hybrid-propulsion vertical-take-off-and landing aircraft. The proceeds from the equity raise today are planned to be used for the development of next-generation aircraft manufacturing capabilities related to the new aircraft, including batteries and composites, with the remainder of the funding going for general corporate purposes. â€œThe opportunity for advanced vertical lift aircraft across defense appears to be substantially larger than I originally expected,â€ said Archer founder and Chief Executive Adam Goldstein. â€œAs a result, we are raising additional capital to help us invest in critical capabilities like composites and batteries to capture this opportunity and more.â€ THANK YOU Archer Aviation raises $300M from Blackrock to expand defense sector focus F5 targets AI-era IT challenges with ADC 3.0 reference architectures Cisco embeds security services in new line of programmable switches Amplitude integrates in-app surveys into its behavioral analysis platform Consortium led by Elon Musk makes $97.4B offer for OpenAI NXP buys Kinara for $307M to power AI workloads at the network edge Archer Aviation raises $300M from Blackrock to expand defense sector focus EMERGING TECH - BY DUNCAN RILEY . 1 MIN AGO F5 targets AI-era IT challenges with ADC 3.0 reference architectures AI - BY DUNCAN RILEY . 2 HOURS AGO Cisco embeds security services in new line of programmable switches INFRA - BY PAUL GILLIN . 5 HOURS AGO Amplitude integrates in-app surveys into its behavioral analysis platform AI - BY PAUL GILLIN . 8 HOURS AGO Consortium led by Elon Musk makes $97.4B offer for OpenAI AI - BY MARIA DEUTSCHER . 14 HOURS AGO NXP buys Kinara for $307M to power AI workloads at the network edge AI - BY MIKE WHEATLEY . 14 HOURS AGO

Title: Bitcoinâ€™s MVRV score nears danger zone â€“ Are short-term holders at risk?
URL: https://ambcrypto.com/bitcoins-mvrv-score-nears-danger-zone-are-short-term-holders-at-risk/
Time Published: 2025-02-11T12:30:44Z
Full Content:
Bitcoinâ€™s short-term MVRV shows investors are still in profit but a drop cannot be ruled out. The Short-Term Holder (STH) MVRV score for Bitcoin [BTC] recently dropped to 1.05. This crucial threshold indicated investors were just above the break-even point. The drop in the MVRV score suggested a potential cooling-off in buying enthusiasm among short-term holders. Despite this decline, the score remaining above 1 implied that the selling pressure may not be as intense yet. This could potentially prevent another drop. Source: Bitcoin Magazine PRO The STHâ€™s approximate cost basis of around $92,000 serves as a critical support level for the market. BTC could drop to $92K, but if it maintains above this cost basis, it could indicate continued confidence among short-term investors, supporting stable prices or an uptrend. Conversely, if the MVRV score falls below 1, it could signify that most STHs are at a loss. This could lead to increased selling pressure as investors attempt to minimize losses. This scenario would put the $92,000 support level at risk of breaking down, possibly triggering a sharper decline in Bitcoinâ€™s price. Further analysis shows that Bitcoin continued with its pattern of interacting frequently with liquidity zones. This pattern persisted, with BTC initially maintaining levels just above the long clusters before inevitably dipping to sweep the liquidity at $95,000. However, the recurrent tests of these liquidity pools suggested a bearish undertone as the price failed to sustain higher levels, especially near the $100,100 short liquidity zone. Source: Hyblock Capital This consistent pull towards lower liquidity zones, now below $94K, signals a potential setup for further drops, potentially down to the $92,000 level, crucial for short-term holders (STHs). If Bitcoin continues this pattern, the $92K level could soon play a pivotal role. Breaking below this level could lead to a shift in market sentiment, possibly causing short-term holders to capitulate, adding downward pressure on the price. Conversely, a successful defense of this level might reinforce confidence, possibly stabilizing or driving up prices as accumulation occurs at these lower levels. Lastly, this drop is supported by the fact that the prices declined despite significant purchases by Michael Saylorâ€™s, MicroStrategy, and BlackRock, alongside the movement of 14,000 dormant Bitcoins. These large transactions might have signaled a potential increase in supply, even if not immediately sold, causing uncertainty and thus a price drop. Source: CryptoQuant Read Bitcoinâ€™s [BTC] Price Prediction 2025â€“2026 If these Bitcoins are seen as long-term holds, not sell-offs, it might suggest less selling pressure. Title: Climate reporting presents brands with an opportunity â€“ if itâ€™s done right
URL: https://www.thedrum.com/opinion/2025/02/11/climate-reporting-presents-brands-with-opportunity-if-it-s-done-right
Time Published: 2025-02-11T07:00:00Z
Full Content:
Advertisement The Drum Network article This content is produced by The Drum Network, a paid-for membership club for CEOs and their agencies who want to share their expertise and grow their business. February 11, 2025 | 8 min read Listen to article 4 min Climate Transition Plans will become crucial for comms teams thanks to the EUâ€™s directive on ESG, says Olly Lawder at Revolt. See these plans as an opportunity to align company values and let the world â€“ and your investors â€“ know about the great work you do. Climate Transition Plans (CTPs) allow companies to creatively communicate their roadmap to net zero, says Lawder / Explore with Joshua via Unsplash The Corporate Sustainability Reporting Directive (CSRD) has raised the bar on Environment, Social, and Governance (ESG) reporting. Itâ€™s estimated that 50,000 companies with a presence in the EU will have to comply with the directive, which requires companies to share information on their monitoring of many ESG issues. The directive is purposefully technical, and this complexity can create a hurdle for communication and engagement. But an opportunity does exist in the shape of the Climate Transition Plan (CTP). The CTP is a mandatory part of the reporting and offers companies an opportunity to creatively communicate their roadmap to net zero. And while marketers may not be creating CTPs, they will certainly be communicating them. The CTP translates sometimes intangible and distant net zero goals into a credible, granular, and powerful business strategy to show to stakeholders. As a mandatory part of CSRD, businesses shouldnâ€™t view the CTP as simply a compliance exercise but as an opportunity to stand out and deliver. Knowing that businesses will be heavily focused on CTPs this year with CSRD coming into force, Revolt conducted quantitative research with over 400 marketing and PR leaders in the US who work at companies with offices in the EU. The aim was to find out just how much marketers know about the directive and whether they will embrace the creative opportunities that CTPs present in their marketing and communications. Reassuringly, we found that nearly 96% of marketeers are aware of CTPs. Given the importance and ramifications of CSRD, we were not surprised by this. However, 30% report that they are either unaware if their company has a CTP or that their company is not developing one. This is a worryingly high percentage, and clearly more needs to be done to ensure that all companies are aware of their climate transition responsibilities. The good news is that all respondents agree â€“ either strongly or somewhat â€“ that CTPs represent good comms opportunities. But when asked about the extent of communications planning around CTPs for the next 12 months, only a third of respondents said they have a specific plan for communicating transition plans. Additionally, 65% reported that CTP communication was not in the broader communications plan, and 71% said they hadnâ€™t budgeted for CTP communications. So, while there is a good understanding of the marketing opportunity with CTPs, there is a real gap in terms of actually making it happen. When we addressed this with respondents, we found a variety of reasons for the slow or lacking movement in communicating CTPs. Concern about accidentally greenwashing is the number one barrier to creatively engaging on climate transition plans. This was followed by a perceived difficulty in engaging audiences in what some consider a â€˜depressing topic,â€™ as well as audiences lacking interest in the subject matter. Other reasons included the complexity of the issues and marketers feeling out of their comfort zone with the topic. However, these barriers can and should be overcome. I believe that there are three things marketers and corporate affairs teams should keep in mind to ensure effective communication of transition plans. Advertisement Climate change isnâ€™t a future concern; itâ€™s already upon us â€“ and investors are looking to invest in businesses that build resilience to climate risks and are ready to take on climate opportunities. Almost 99% of leading global insurance companies have now set a low-carbon transition objective within their investment portfolios, according to Blackrock. While CTPs existed before CSRD, they lacked granularity. The new directive will create a groundswell of information that investors will look at, including the disclosure of climate-related risks, transition-related opportunities, investment plans for low-carbon technologies, impacts on staff, scenario-planning, and financial allocation for activity. The CTP is an opportunity to translate your net-zero strategy into a powerful investment story â€“ a story of resilience, adaptability, and competitive advantage that only your business can offer investors. It forms part of an ongoing dialogue and is a way to update investors on your transition progress. Advertisement Every stakeholder plays a role in delivering on your CTP, but none is as important as your employees. Employees are potential champions and crucial implementers of your transition strategies. Employees play a role across all three principles of the CTP â€“ Ambition, Action, and Accountability â€“ and they act as change agents who can ensure the CTP does not just live in a document. Showcasing how individual roles directly contribute to broader goals creates a compelling narrative that will help retain talent who see sustainability as a personal mission rather than a corporate imperative. To transition successfully, businesses will need people with the right skill sets and CTP comms that hero employees â€“ and show that measurable impact can help to attract future talent who value sustainability. Catch up on the most important stories of the day, curated by our editorial team. Stay up to date with a curated digest of the most important marketing stories and expert insights from our global team. Learn how to pitch to our editors and get published on The Drum. For effective transition planning, businesses must engage their value chain because, in most cases, Scope 3 emissions (all indirect emissions relating to business activity, excluding utilities) represent the largest portion of a businessâ€™s carbon footprint. So, while CTPs are individual to each business, they can only be achieved with systemic change across suppliers and geographies. Itâ€™s important that CTPs deliver and communicate a detailed and quantifiable picture of the value chain, including its most opaque areas. View the CTP not as a supplier compliance checklist but rather a communication device to highlight a shared purpose between your business and your value chain. Move toward storytelling that demonstrates genuine partnership and success stories, collaborative decarbonization efforts, and, in turn, acts as a confidence-builder for other stakeholders too, including investors. CTPs will become a critical element of the comms suite around reporting going forward, and with the first CSRD disclosures being made in 2025, the time to engage is now. Plans will be scrutinized, so get ready to be vocal and to defend and uphold them, but do not see your comms solely as a form of defense. Instead, engaging and ambitious comms are your opportunity to inspire stakeholders, catalyze investment and innovation, and ensure your plans progress into reality. Revolt The world is on fire.
